рез-реирел рдЪрд╛рддрдирдГред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реЛрдореМред рдЬрдЧрддреА, рео-резрек, резрем-резрен, резреп, реиреи, реирек рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН, реиреж,реирей рднреБрд░рд┐рдХреН, реирел рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреНред

Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[C─Бtana.тАФpa├▒caviс╣Е┼Ыakam. mantroktadevatyam. j─Бgatam: 8-14, 16, 17, 19, 22, 24. triс╣гс╣нubh; 20, 23. bhurij; 25. anuс╣гс╣нubh.]

Whitney

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. (with exchange of order between 4 and 5, and between 19 and 20). It is, with no change of order of verses, and with only few and insignificant variants, RV. vii. 104; not a verse occurs further in any other text, so far as known.

тМКNo ritual use of the hymn is prescribed either by K─Бu┼Ы. or by V─Бit. But the comm. regards this hymn as used with the preceding one in a variety of practices: see h. 3.тМЛ

Translations

Translated: by the RV. translators; and as AV. hymn by Henry, 10, 47; Griffith, i. 396.

Griffith

режрез рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╕реЛрдорд╛ рддрдкрддрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, burn the demon, oppress (ubj) [him]; put
    (arpay-) down, ye two bulls, them that thrive in darkness; crush away,
    scorch down the fools (ac├нt); slay, push, pin (┼Ы─Б) down the
    devourers.
Notes

Tamovс╣Ы╠Бdh may be (so Ludwig) ‘increaser of darkness.’ The comm. has
nothing better than hiс╣Еs to suggest for ubj.

Griffith

Indra and Soma, burn, destroy the demon foe! Send downward, O ye Bulls, those who add gloom to gloom. Annihilate the fools, slay them and burn them up: chase them away from us, pierce the voracious fiends.

Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, against тМКabh├нтМЛ the evil-plotter, the evil, let
    heat boil all up тМКsam-yasтМЛ like a fiery pot; assign unavoidable hate
    unto the brahman-hating, flesh-eating kim─лd├нn of terrible aspect.
Notes

The construction and meaning of the first half-verse are doubtful; the
comm. glosses yayastu with simple gacchatu. RV. has agniv─Б╠Бс╣Е
instead of -m─Б╠Бс╣Е in b. In our edition, the accent-sign which should
stand under gni in this word has slipped to the right, under m─Бс╣Е.
тМКHere W. seems to take sam as intensive and to render its force by
“all up.” Neither in BR. nor in the Index is it joined with yas: but
cf. saс╣Б-y─Бsa.тМЛ

Griffith

Let sin, Indra and Soma! round the wicked boil, like as a cald- ron set amid the flames of fire. Against the foe of prayer, eater of gory flesh, the fearful-eyed Kimidin, keep perpetual hate.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, pierce ye the evil-doers within their hiding-place
    (vavr├б), in untenable darkness, whence there shall not come up again
    any one soever of them; be that your furious might unto overpowering.
Notes

RV. reads at beginning of c y├бth─Б n─Б╠Б тАЩtaс╕е p├║n-. In our edition
read duс╣гkс╣Ы╠Бto in a.

Griffith

Indra and Soma, plunge the wicked in the depth, yea, cast them into darkness that hath no support, So that not one of them may ever thence return: so may your wrathful might prevail and conquer them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, cause to roll (vс╣Ыt) from the sky the deadly
    weapon, from the earth also, a shattering for the evil-plotter; shape
    out from the mountains (p├бrvata) the noisy one, wherewith ye burn down
    the increasing demon.
Notes

The comm. glosses svary├а with svaraс╣З─Бrha. Ppp. has the easier
reading pra harataс╣Б for vartayatam in a.

Griffith

Indra and Soma, hurl your deadly crushing bolt down on the wicked fiend from heaven and from the earth. Yea, fashion from the big clouds your celestial dart wherewith ye burn to death the waxing demon race.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, cause [it] to roll forth from the sky; with
    fireheated, stone-smiting, unaging heat-weapons do ye pierce the

Notes

Ppp. reads divas for yuvam in b; the comm. has in d
niс╕еsvaram, which would be a good reading, but is against the

Griffith

Indra and Soma, cast ye downward from the sky your deadly bolts of stone burning with fiery flame, Eternal, scorching darts. Plunge the voracious fiends within the depth, and let them pass without a sound.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra-and-Soma, be there about you on all sides this prayer
    (mat├н), as a girth [about] two vigorous (v─Бj├нn) horses, the
    invocation (h├│tr─Б) that I send forth to you with wisdom; these acts of
    worship (br├бhman) quicken ye like two lords of men.
Notes

RV. reads in d nс╣Ыp├бt─л тАЩva, as the meter demands, and so do our
P.M.W.R.T.K. and part of SPP’s authorities, also the comm., and Ppp.,
and this is, almost beyond question, the true text; but SPP. adopts in
his edition nс╣Ыp├бt─л iva, with the remainder (a majority) of his
saс╣Бhit─Б authorities. The pada-reading is probably nс╣Ыp├бt─л iv├й тАЩti
nс╣Ыp├бt─лре░iva, as all the pada-mss. except our Bp. (both copies) appear
to read, and as the RV. pada reads; but we should altogether expect
nс╣Ыp├бt─л тАЩv├й тАЩti nс╣Ыp├бt─лре░iva, as Bp. reads. The anomaly of the addition
of iti after iva instead of after nс╣Ыp├бt─л (first time) is noted in
Pr─Бt. i. 82 c; the Pr─Бt. takes no notice of the exceptional combination
nс╣Ыpat─л тАЩvaтАФwhich is, to be sure, an argument against its right to
stand in the saс╣Бhit─Б-text: see note to Pr─Бt. iii. 33. The retention of
dental n in hin├│mi after pari is prescribed by Pr─Бt. iii. 88. Ppp.
reads instead pra hiс╣Зomi. тМКCf. Geldner, Ved. Stud. ii. 134.тМЛ

Griffith

Indra and Soma, let this hymn control you both, even as the girth encompasses two vigorous steeds The song of praise which I with wisdom offer you. Do ye, as Lords of men, animate these my prayers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Remember ye with [your] rapid courses; smite the haters, the
    destructive demoniacs; O Indra-and-Soma, let there not be ease (sug├б)
    for the evil-doer, the hater that at any time vexes me.
Notes

RV. reads, in d, nas for m─Б, and druh─Б╠Б for druh├║s. Ppp. ends
with (for abhi…) api k─Б cid ud ┼лhuс╕е. The retention of dental s
in pr├бti smar- is by Pr─Бt. ii. 102; the passage is there quoted in the
commentary. Our comm. glosses tujayadbhis with balavadbhis, and
attenuates the difficult prati smareth─Бm to prati gacchatam.

Griffith

In your impetuous manner think ye both thereon: destroy those evil spirits, kill the treacherous fiends. Indra and Soma, let the wicked have no bliss whoso at any time- attacks and injures us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever reviles with untrue speeches me walking with simple mindтАФlike
    waters grasped with the fist, let the speaker of what is not be
    [himself] non-existent, O Indra.
Notes

The comm. glosses abhic├бс╣гс╣нe with abhi┼Ы─Бpaс╣Б karoti. The long initial
vowel of ─Б╠Бsatas (p. ├бsataс╕е) is by Pr─Бt. iii. 21, iv. 90; the passage
is there quoted.

Griffith

Whoso accuses me with words of falsehood when I pursue my way with guileless spirit, May he, the speaker of untruth, be, Indra! like water which the hollowed hand compresses.

Translation
  1. They who distract (vi-hс╣Ы) with [their] courses him of simple
    intent, or who spoil at their will (svadh─Б╠Бbhis) what is excellentтАФlet
    Soma either deliver them up to the serpent, or let him set them in the
    lap of perdition.

The comm. declares svadh─Б in b an annan─Бma, and renders
svadh─Бbhis by ann─Бir nimittabh┼лt─Бiс╕е, ‘for food’! An accent-mark is
wanting in our text over the ya of d┼лс╣г├бyanti in b.

Griffith

Those who destroy, as is their wont, the simple, and with their evil natures harm the righteous, May Soma give them over to the serpent, or to the lap of Nirriti consign them.

O Agni, whosoever seeks to injure the essence of our food, kine, steeds, or bodies, May he, the adversary, thief, and robber, sink to destruction,. both himself and offspring.

резрез рдкрд░рдГ рд╕реЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Be he far away, with self and with posterity, be he beneath all the
    three earths, let his glory dry up, ye gods, who by day and who by night
    tries to harm me.
Notes

RV. reads in d nas instead of m─Б.

Griffith

May he be swept away, himself and children; may all the three earths press him down beneath them. May his fair glory, O ye Gods, be blighted, who in the day or night would fain destroy us.

резреи рд╕реБрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреБрд╖реЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. It is easy of understanding for a knowing man (j├бna) [that] true
    and untrue words (v├бcas) are at variance; of them what is true,
    whichever is more right, that Soma verily favors; he smites the untrue.
Notes

Ppp. reads paspс╣Ы┼Ы─Бte at end of b.

Griffith

The prudent finds it easy to distinguish the true and false: their words oppose each other. Of these two that which is the true and honest Soma protects, and brings the false to nothing.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Soma by no means furthers the wicked [man], nor the kshatr├нya
    who maintains [anything] falsely; he smites the demon; he smites the
    speaker of untruth; both lie within reach of Indra.
Notes
Griffith

Never doth Soma aid and guide the wicked or him who falsely claims the Warrior’s title. He slays the fiend and him who speaks untruly: both lie entan- gled in the noose of Indra.

Translation
  1. If I am one of false gods, or if I put upon (? api-┼лh) the gods
    what is vain, O AgniтАФwhy art thou angry with us, O J─Бtavedas? let them
    of hateful speech obtain (sac) misery of thee.

RV. reads ─Б╠Бsa instead of ├бsmi at end of a. The comm. renders
te in d as if it were t├й; for the difficult apy-┼лh├й he gives
simply vah─Бmi (moghaс╣Б vyarthaс╣Б dev─Бn stotavy─Бn yaс╣гс╣нavy─Бс╣Е┼Ы ca apy┼лhe
vah─Бmi).

As if I worshipped deities of falsehood, or thought vain thoughts about the Gods, O Agni! Why art thou angry with us, Jatavedas? Destruction fall on those who lie against thee!

резрел рдЕрджреНрдпрд╛ рдореБрд░реАрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. May I die today if I am a sorcerer, or if I have burnt (tap) a
    man’s lifetime; then let him be divided from ten heroes who vainly says
    to me “thou sorcerer.”
Notes

The comm. glosses v─лr─Бis with putr─Бis, which is probably its virtual
meaning: ‘may he lose ten heroic sons.’ Our pada-text differs from
that of RV. by dividing da┼Ы├бре░bhiс╕е in c. Ppp. reads p─Бuruс╣гasya in
b.

Griffith

So may I die this day if I have harassed any man’s life, or if I be a demon. Yea, may he lose all his ten sons together who with false tongue hath called me Yatudhana.

Translation
  1. Whoever to me that am no sorcerer (├бy─Бtu) says “thou sorcerer,” or
    whatever demoniac says “I am pure (┼Ы├║ci)"тАФlet Indra smite him with a
    great deadly weapon; may he fall lowest of every creature.
Notes

├Бy─Бtu doubtless literally ’that have no y─Бt├║ or familiar demon’
(though the proper accent in such case would be ay─Бt├║), opposite of
y─Бtum├бnt ‘possessing such a y─Бt├║,’ or y─Бtudh─Б╠Бna ‘holding or
containing such.’

Griffith

May Indra slay him with a mighty weapon, and let the vilest of all creatures perish, The fiend who says that he is pure, who calls me a demon though devoid of demon nature.

She too who wanders like an owl at night-time, hiding her body in her guile and malice, May she fall downward into endless caverns. May press-stones with loud ring destroy the demons.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Scatter yourselves, O Maruts, among the people (vikс╣г├║); seek,
    seize, crush (sam-piс╣г) the demoniacs, who, becoming birds, fly in the
    nights, or who have put defilements (r├нpas) on the heavenly sacrifice.
Notes

RV. has bh┼лtv─л╠Б in c. SPP. reads i3cchata in a, because the
great majority of his authorities give it. This is contrary to the
established usage of both RV. and AV. (but in accordance with that of
SV.), although in nearly every such case a part of the mss. lengthen the
vowel; part of ours do the same here, as elsewhere. The comm. glosses
ripas with hiс╣Еsas; and dadhire with dh─Бrayanti!

Griffith

Spread out, ye Maruts, search among the people: seize ye and grind the Rakshasas to pieces, Who fly abroad, transformed to birds, at night-time, and sully and pollute our holy worship.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Cause the stone to roll forth from the sky, O Indra; [it,]
    sharpened by Soma, do thou wholly sharpen, O liberal one; from before,
    from away, from below, from above, do thou smite upon the demoniacs with
    a mountain.
Notes

RV. reads in a ├б┼Ыm- after div├│, and some of SPP’s authorities do
the same. RV. has also pr─Б╠Бkt─Бd ├бp─Бkt─Бd and ├║dakt─Бd in c; the
directions admit also of being understood as from east, west, south, and
north.

Griffith

Hurl down from heaven thy bolt of stone, O Indra: sharpen it, Maghavan, made keen by Soma. Forward, behind, and from above and under, smite down the demons with thy rocky weapon.

реиреж рдПрдд рдЙ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Here fly these dog-sorcerers (┼Ыv├бy─Бtu); Indra the unharmable they
    the harm-seeking seek to harm; the mighty one (┼Ыakr├б) sharpens his
    deadly weapon for the treacherous ones (p├н┼Ыuna); now may he let fly
    (sс╣Ыj) the thunderbolt at the sorcerers (y─Бtum├бnt).
Notes

The epithets like ┼Ыv├бy─Бtu in this verse and below in vs. 22 seem by
their accent (and by comparison with y─Бtum├бnt and y─Бtudh─Б╠Бna) to
signify strictly ‘one having a dog (etc.) for his familiar demon.’ The
comm. glosses with ┼Ыvar┼лpadh─Бriс╣Зaс╕е ┼Ыvasahit─Б [v─Б]. Ppp. combines
at end of b -vo ad─Бbhyam.

Griffith

They fly, the demon dogs, and, bent on mischief, fain would they harm indomitable Indra. Sakra makes sharp his weapon for the wicked: now let him cast his bolt at fiendish wizards.

Translation
  1. Indra was the crusher-away of the familiar demons (y─Бt├║), of the
    oblation-disturbers, of them who strive to win upon [it]; let the
    mighty one (┼Ыakr├б) attack them that are demoniacs as an ax the woods,
    splitting [them] like vessels.
Notes

RV. reads eti in d, and no small share of the AV. mss. (the
majority of SPP’s) do the same (including our P.s.m.I.D.R.p.m.Kp.); both
editions give etu. The AV. pada-text, like the RV., divides and
accents in b abh├н: ─Бре░v├нv─Бsat─Бm. The Petersburg Lexicons treat the
abhi as if in direct combination with the participle; and they
translate ‘approach with hostile intent,’ which is highly arbitrary. The
comm. gives no aid, rendering simply abhimukhaс╣Б gacchat─Бm. Ppp. reads
in b -mat─лn─Бm. тМКW. would probably have changed “crusher-away” to
“demolisher” on the revision.тМЛ

Griffith

Indra hath ever been the fiends’ destroyer who spoil oblations of the Gods’ invokers. Yea, Sakra, like an axe that splits the timber, assails and sma- shes them like earthen vessels.

Translation
  1. The owl-sorcerer, the owlet-(?)sorcerer smite thou, the dog-sorcerer
    and the cuckoo-sorcerer, the eagle-(? suparс╣З├б)sorcerer and the
    vulture-sorcererтАФdo thou destroy (pra-mс╣Ыс╣З) the demon, O Indra, as if
    with a mill-stone.
Notes

As to the renderings of these various names for sorcerers, see under vs.
20. For ┼Ыu┼Ыul┼лka- Ppp. has ┼Ыul┼лka-, the comm. ┼Ыi┼Ыul┼лka-. The
translation of it is a mere guess, to avoid transferring the word.

Griffith

Destroy the fiend shaped like an owl or owlet, destroy him in. the form of dog or cuckoo. Destroy him shaped as eagle or as vulture: as with a stone, O Indra, crush the demon.

Indra destroy the demon, male and female, joying and triumph- ing in arts of magic! Let the fools’ gods with bent necks fall and perish, and see no. more the Sun when he arises.

Translation
  1. Look thou on; look abroad; O Soma, Indra also, watch ye; hurl ye the
    deadly weapon at the demons, the thunderbolt at the sorcerers
    (y─Бtum├бnt).
Notes

Anukr. says tur─лyam ─Бhur iha pa├▒caviс╣Е┼Ыakam.тМЛ

Griffith

Look, each one, hither, look around. Indra and Soma, watch ye well. Cast forth your weapon at the fiends: against the sorcerers hurl your bolt.
